</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Functions" title="Template:Functions"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Functions" title="Template talk:Functions"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Functions&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, a <b>function</b> from a <a href="/wiki/Set_(mathematics)" title="Set (mathematics)">set</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> to a set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span> assigns to each element of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> exactly one element of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halmos_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-halmos-1">[1]</a></sup> The set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> is called the <a href="/wiki/Domain_of_a_function" title="Domain of a function">domain</a> of the function<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and the set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span> is called the <a href="/wiki/Codomain" title="Codomain">codomain</a> of the function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-codomain_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-codomain-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="The current citations do not match the text of the article. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The earliest known approach to the notion of function can be traced back to works of Persian mathematicians <a href="/wiki/Al-Biruni" title="Al-Biruni">Al-Biruni</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sharaf_al-Din_al-Tusi" title="Sharaf al-Din al-Tusi">Sharaf al-Din al-Tusi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Functions were originally the idealization of how a varying quantity depends on another quantity. For example, the position of a <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a> is a <i>function</i> of time. <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_function_concept" title="History of the function concept">Historically</a>, the concept was elaborated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infinitesimal_calculus" title="Infinitesimal calculus">infinitesimal calculus</a> at the end of the 17th century, and, until the 19th century, the functions that were considered were <a href="/wiki/Differentiable_function" title="Differentiable function">differentiable</a> (that is, they had a high degree of regularity). The concept of a function was formalized at the end of the 19th century in terms of <a href="/wiki/Set_theory" title="Set theory">set theory</a>, and this greatly enlarged the domains of application of the concept.
</p><p>A function is most often denoted by letters such as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">g</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">h</span>, and the value of a function <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> at an element <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> of its domain is denoted by <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span>; the numerical value resulting from the <i>function evaluation</i> at a particular input value is denoted by replacing <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> with this value; for example, the value of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> at <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> = 4</span> is denoted by <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(4)</span>. When the function is not named and is represented by an <a href="/wiki/Expression_(mathematics)" title="Expression (mathematics)">expression</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">E</span>, the value of the function at, say, <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> = 4</span> may be denoted by <span class="texhtml"><i>E</i>|<sub><i>x</i>=4</sub></span>. For example, the value at <span class="texhtml">4</span> of the function that maps <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (x+1)^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (x+1)^{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="(x+1)^2" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/29e98be23926b1484d39e456f7629dc26a13179d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.196ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> may be denoted by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \left.(x+1)^{2}\right\vert _{x=4}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mrow>
<mo fence="true" stretchy="true" symmetric="true"></mo>
<mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>

</msup>

<mi>x</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>4</mn>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \left.(x+1)^{2}\right\vert _{x=4}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \left.(x+1)^{2}\right\vert _{x=4}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87465e3b93aec1223e1bf9896d0235d5886f21ab" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:12.116ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span> (which results in <span class="texhtml">25).</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>A function is uniquely represented by the set of all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pair_(mathematics)" title="Pair (mathematics)">pairs</a> <span class="texhtml">(<i>x</i>, <i>f</i> (<i>x</i>))</span>, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Graph_of_a_function" title="Graph of a function">graph of the function</a></i>, a popular means of illustrating the function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[note 1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> When the domain and the codomain are sets of real numbers, each such pair may be thought of as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinates" title="Cartesian coordinates">Cartesian coordinates</a> of a point in the plane.
</p><p>Functions are widely used in <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, and in most fields of mathematics. It has been said that functions are "the central objects of investigation" in most fields of mathematics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpivak200839_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpivak200839-8">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Function_machine2.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="189" data-file-width="191" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Function_machine2.svg/220px-Function_machine2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Function_machine2.svg/330px-Function_machine2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Function_machine2.svg/440px-Function_machine2.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Function_machine2.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Schematic depiction of a function described metaphorically as a "machine" or "<a href="/wiki/Black_box" title="Black box">black box</a>" that for each input yields a corresponding output</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Graph_of_example_function.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Graph_of_example_function.svg/220px-Graph_of_example_function.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Graph_of_example_function.svg/330px-Graph_of_example_function.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Graph_of_example_function.svg/440px-Graph_of_example_function.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Graph_of_example_function.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The red curve is the <a href="/wiki/Graph_of_a_function" title="Graph of a function">graph of a function</a>, because any <a href="/wiki/Vertical_line_test" title="Vertical line test">vertical line</a> has exactly one crossing point with the curve.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Function_color_example_3.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="321" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Function_color_example_3.svg/220px-Function_color_example_3.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Function_color_example_3.svg/330px-Function_color_example_3.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Function_color_example_3.svg/440px-Function_color_example_3.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Function_color_example_3.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A function that associates any of the four colored shapes to its color.</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg/220px-Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg/330px-Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg/440px-Injection_keine_Injektion_2a.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Diagram of a function, with domain <span class="texhtml"><i>X</i> = {1, 2, 3}</span> and codomain <span class="texhtml"><i>Y</i> = {A, B, C, D}</span>, which is defined by the set of ordered pairs <span class="texhtml">{(1, D), (2, C), (3, C)} </span>. The image/range is the set <span class="texhtml">{C, D} </span>.
<br/><hr style="height:8pt; visibility:hidden"/>
<hr/><hr style="height:8pt; visibility:hidden"/></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg/220px-Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg/330px-Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg/440px-Injection_keine_Injektion_1.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">This diagram, representing the set of pairs <span class="texhtml">{(1,D), (2,B), (2,C)} </span>, does <i>not</i> define a function. One reason is that 2 is the first element in more than one ordered pair, <span class="texhtml">(2, B)</span> and <span class="texhtml">(2, C)</span>, of this set.  Two other reasons, also sufficient by themselves, is that neither 3 nor 4 are first elements (input) of any ordered pair therein.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>A <b>function</b> from a <a href="/wiki/Set_(mathematics)" title="Set (mathematics)">set</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> to a set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span> is an assignment of an element of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span> to each element of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span>. The set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> is called the <a href="/wiki/Domain_of_a_function" title="Domain of a function">domain</a> of the function and the set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span> is called the <a href="/wiki/Codomain" title="Codomain">codomain</a> of the function.
</p><p>A function, its domain, and its codomain, are declared by the notation <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>: <i>X</i>→<i>Y</i></span>, and the value of a function <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> at an element <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span>, denoted by <span class="texhtml"><i>f(x)</i></span>, is called the <i>image</i> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> under <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span>, or the <i>value</i> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> applied to the <i>argument</i> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>. 
</p><p>Functions are also called <i><a href="/wiki/Map_(mathematics)" title="Map (mathematics)">maps</a></i> or <i>mappings</i>, though some authors make some distinction between "maps" and "functions" (see <a href="#Other_terms">§ Other terms</a>).
</p><p>Two functions <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">g</span> are equal if their domain and codomain sets are the same and their output values agree on the whole domain. More formally, given  <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>: <i>X</i> → <i>Y</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>g</i>: <i>X</i> → <i>Y</i></span>, we have <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i> = <i>g</i></span> if and only if <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>) = <i>g</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> for all <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> ∈ <i>X</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaplan197225_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaplan197225-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[note 2]</a></sup>
</p><p>The domain and codomain are not always explicitly given when a function is defined, and, without some (possibly difficult) computation, one might only know that the domain is contained in a larger set. Typically, this occurs in <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_analysis" title="Mathematical analysis">mathematical analysis</a>, where "a function <span class="nowrap">from <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> to <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">Y</span> "</span> often refers to a function that may have a proper subset<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[note 3]</a></sup> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> as domain. For example, a "function from the reals to the reals" may refer to a <a href="/wiki/Real-valued_function" title="Real-valued function">real-valued</a> function of a <a href="/wiki/Function_of_a_real_variable" title="Function of a real variable">real variable</a>. However, a "function from the reals to the reals" does not mean that the domain of the function is the whole set of the <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real numbers</a>, but only that the domain is a set of real numbers that contains a non-empty <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_interval" title="Open interval">open interval</a>. Such a function is then called a <a href="/wiki/Partial_function" title="Partial function">partial function</a>. For example, if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> is a function that has the real numbers as domain and codomain, then a function mapping the value <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> to the value <span class="texhtml"><i>g</i>(<i>x</i>) = <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1050945101">.mw-parser-output .sfrac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .sfrac.tion,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .tion{display:inline-block;vertical-align:-0.5em;font-size:85%;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .num,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{display:block;line-height:1em;margin:0 0.1em}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{border-top:1px solid}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="sfrac tion" role="math"><span class="num">1</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span></span></span> is a function <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">g</span> from the reals to the reals, whose domain is the set of the reals <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>, such that <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>) ≠ 0</span>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Range_of_a_function" title="Range of a function">range</a> or <a href="/wiki/Image_(mathematics)" title="Image (mathematics)">image</a> of a function is the set of the <a href="/wiki/Image_(mathematics)" title="Image (mathematics)">images</a> of all elements in the domain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EOM_Function_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-EOM_Function-12">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T&amp;K_Calc_p.3_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-T&amp;K_Calc_p.3-13">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trench_RA_pp.30-32_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trench_RA_pp.30-32-14">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TBB_RA_pp.A4-A5_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-TBB_RA_pp.A4-A5-15">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Total.2C_univalent_relation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Total,_univalent_relation">Total, univalent relation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Total, univalent relation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Any subset of the <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_product" title="Cartesian product">Cartesian product</a> of two sets <span class="texhtml"><i>X</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>Y</i></span> defines a <a href="/wiki/Binary_relation" title="Binary relation">binary relation</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>R</i> ⊆ <i>X</i> × <i>Y</i></span> between these two sets. It is immediate that an arbitrary relation may contain pairs that violate the necessary conditions for a function given above.
</p><p>A binary relation is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Univalent_relation" title="Univalent relation">univalent</a> (also called right-unique) if
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \forall x\in X,\forall y\in Y,\forall z\in Y,\quad ((x,y)\in R\land (x,z)\in R)\implies y=z.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \forall x\in X,\forall y\in Y,\forall z\in Y,\quad ((x,y)\in R\land (x,z)\in R)\implies y=z.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \forall x\in X,\forall y\in Y,\forall z\in Y,\quad ((x,y)\in R\land (x,z)\in R)\implies y=z.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/05ca3e4423ee56195ceb7c57afdd29a6d982b21e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:63.49ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>A binary relation is <a href="/wiki/Total_relation" title="Total relation">total</a> if
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \forall x\in X,\exists y\in Y,\quad (x,y)\in R.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∀<!-- ∀ --></mi>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>∈<!-- ∈ --></mo>
<mi>X</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∃<!-- ∃ --></mi>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>∈<!-- ∈ --></mo>
<mi>Y</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mspace width="1em"></mspace>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>∈<!-- ∈ --></mo>
<mi>R</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \forall x\in X,\exists y\in Y,\quad (x,y)\in R.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \forall x\in X,\exists y\in Y,\quad (x,y)\in R.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a33f44183452b5378f25004fc9dfb7087266c0e7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:29.475ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Partial_function" title="Partial function">partial function</a> is a binary relation that is univalent, and a <b>function</b> is a binary relation that is univalent and total.
</p><p>Various properties of functions and function composition may be reformulated in the language of relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RM_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-RM-16">[13]</a></sup> For example, a function is <a href="/wiki/Injective_function" title="Injective function">injective</a> if the <a href="/wiki/Converse_relation" title="Converse relation">converse relation</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>R</i><sup>T</sup> ⊆ <i>Y</i> × <i>X</i></span> is univalent, where the converse relation is defined as <span class="texhtml"><i>R</i><sup>T</sup> = {(<i>y</i>, <i>x</i>) | (<i>x</i>, <i>y</i>) ∈ <i>R</i>}.</span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Set_exponentiation">Set exponentiation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Set exponentiation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Exponentiation#Sets_as_exponents" title="Exponentiation">Exponentiation § Sets as exponents</a></div>
<p>The set of all functions from a set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> to a set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>Y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="Y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/961d67d6b454b4df2301ac571808a3538b3a6d3f" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is commonly denoted as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Y^{X},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mi>X</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y^{X},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle Y^{X},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/754c028ad6a5e8ab485b93a831115fb5df068cee" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.179ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>which is read as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>Y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="Y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/961d67d6b454b4df2301ac571808a3538b3a6d3f" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> <i>to the power</i> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>This notation is the same as the notation for the <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_product" title="Cartesian product">Cartesian product</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Indexed_family" title="Indexed family">family</a> of copies of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>Y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="Y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/961d67d6b454b4df2301ac571808a3538b3a6d3f" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> indexed by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Y^{X}=\prod _{x\in X}Y.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>The identity of these two notations is motivated by the fact that a function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> can be identified with the element of the Cartesian product such that the component of index <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f(x)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/202945cce41ecebb6f643f31d119c514bec7a074" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.418ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>When <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle Y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>Y</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>X</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y^{X}}</annotation>
</semantics>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 2^{X}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="2^X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/59a83de58939a4ef8e4837ab6dd554da4278f557" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.795ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> and called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Powerset" title="Powerset">powerset</a> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span>. It can be identified with the set of all <a href="/wiki/Subset" title="Subset">subsets</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notation">Notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are various standard ways for denoting functions. The most commonly used notation is functional notation, which is the first notation described below.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Functional_notation">Functional notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Functional notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In functional notation, the function is immediately given a name, such as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span>, and its definition is given by what <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> does to the explicit argument <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>, using a formula in terms of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>. For example, the function which takes a real number as input and outputs that number plus 1 is denoted by
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)=x+1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)=x+1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)=x+1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/65b53f15b168cb5ab622af5026b0a874e94a8c32" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.849ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.</dd></dl>
<p>If a function is defined in this notation, its domain and codomain are implicitly taken to both be <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, the set of real numbers. If the formula cannot be evaluated at all real numbers, then the domain is implicitly taken to be the maximal subset of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> on which the formula can be evaluated; see <a href="/wiki/Domain_of_a_function" title="Domain of a function">Domain of a function</a>.
</p><p>A more complicated example is the function
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)=\sin(x^{2}+1)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>sin</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)=\sin(x^{2}+1)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)=\sin(x^{2}+1)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ba3b1c9d9e56b3327baceebfd1e530cc5b132a06" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.568ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>.</dd></dl>
<p>In this example, the function <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> takes a real number as input, squares it, then adds 1 to the result, then takes the sine of the result, and returns the final result as the output.
</p><p>When the symbol denoting the function consists of several characters and no ambiguity may arise, the parentheses of functional notation might be omitted. For example, it is common to write <span class="texhtml">sin <i>x</i></span> instead of <span class="texhtml">sin(<i>x</i>)</span>.
</p><p>Functional notation was first used by <a href="/wiki/Leonhard_Euler" title="Leonhard Euler">Leonhard Euler</a> in 1734.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> Some widely used functions are represented by a symbol consisting of several letters (usually two or three, generally an abbreviation of their name). In this case, a <a href="/wiki/Roman_type" title="Roman type">roman type</a> is customarily used instead, such as "<span class="texhtml">sin</span>" for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sine_function" title="Sine function">sine function</a>, in contrast to italic font for single-letter symbols.
</p><p>When using this notation, one often encounters the <a href="/wiki/Abuse_of_notation" title="Abuse of notation">abuse of notation</a> whereby the notation <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> can refer to the value of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> at <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>, or to the function itself. If the variable <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> was previously declared, then the notation <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> unambiguously means the value of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> at <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>. Otherwise, it is useful to understand the notation as being both simultaneously; this allows one to denote composition of two functions <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">g</span> in a succinct manner by the notation <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>g</i>(<i>x</i>))</span>.
</p><p>However, distinguishing <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">f</span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> can become important in cases where functions themselves serve as inputs for other functions. (A function taking another function as an input is termed a <i><a href="/wiki/Functional_(mathematics)" title="Functional (mathematics)">functional</a></i>.) Other approaches of notating functions, detailed below, avoid this problem but are less commonly used.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrow_notation">Arrow notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Arrow notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Arrow notation defines the rule of a function inline, without requiring a name to be given to the function. For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto x+1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">↦<!-- ↦ --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto x+1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x\mapsto x+1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/092c91a7a2ccb9481d3da9c5e59cd410c66dd87f" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:10.276ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is the function which takes a real number as input and outputs that number plus 1. Again a domain and codomain of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is implied.
</p><p>The domain and codomain can also be explicitly stated, for example:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\operatorname {sqr} \colon \mathbb {Z} &amp;\to \mathbb {Z} \\x&amp;\mapsto x^{2}.\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\operatorname {sqr} \colon \mathbb {Z} &amp;\to \mathbb {Z} \\x&amp;\mapsto x^{2}.\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c83da8e3fd28ad40fade38a4a75b3de3be02e792" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:13.036ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>This defines a function <span class="texhtml">sqr</span> from the integers to the integers that returns the square of its input.
</p><p>As a common application of the arrow notation, suppose <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f\colon X\times X\to Y;\;(x,t)\mapsto f(x,t)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

The map in question could be denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x,t_{0})}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

The expression <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x,t_{0})}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Index_notation">Index notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Index notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Index notation is often used instead of functional notation. That is, instead of writing <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i> (<i>x</i>)</span>, one writes <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f_{x}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>f</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f_{x}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f_{x}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/04a7e56cbda7f3fa285ea6a6500af7901cbf58d9" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.959ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>
</p><p>This is typically the case for functions whose domain is the set of the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a>. Such a function is called a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sequence_(mathematics)" title="Sequence (mathematics)">sequence</a>, and, in this case the element <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>f</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f_{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f_{n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b2702450f0458a5e01a698e248af552a7fab2b50" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.358ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is called the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th element of sequence.
</p><p>The index notation is also often used for distinguishing some variables called <a href="/wiki/Parameter" title="Parameter">parameters</a> from the "true variables". In fact, parameters are specific variables that are considered as being fixed during the study of a problem.  For example, the map <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x,t)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>x</mi>

<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>t</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x,t)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x,t)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e82a8366e1505166fcef3257f1fec8f056140157" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.235ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> (see above) would be denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f_{t}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>f</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f_{t}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f_{t}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/874c306411e808e8191e8aeb95e3440e1c68d6e9" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.965ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> using index notation, if we define the collection of maps <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f_{t}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f_{t}}</annotation>
</semantics>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dot_notation">Dot notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dot notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the notation
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">↦<!-- ↦ --></mo>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x),}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x\mapsto f(x),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3322446e350dec66a9be262d198979af3d1c0da0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.008ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>
the symbol <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> does not represent any value, it is simply a <a href="/wiki/Placeholder_name" title="Placeholder name">placeholder</a> meaning that, if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is replaced by any value on the left of the arrow, it should be replaced by the same value on the right of the arrow. Therefore, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> may be replaced by any symbol, often an <a href="/wiki/Interpunct" title="Interpunct">interpunct</a> "<span class="texhtml"> ⋅ </span>". This may be useful for distinguishing the function <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i> (⋅)</span> from its value <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i> (<i>x</i>)</span> at <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>.
</p><p>For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a(\cdot )^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialized_notations">Specialized notations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Specialized notations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are other, specialized notations for functions in sub-disciplines of mathematics.  For example, in <a href="/wiki/Linear_algebra" title="Linear algebra">linear algebra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Functional_analysis" title="Functional analysis">functional analysis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linear_form" title="Linear form">linear forms</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vector_(mathematics_and_physics)" title="Vector (mathematics and physics)">vectors</a> they act upon are denoted using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dual_pair" title="Dual pair">dual pair</a> to show the underlying <a href="/wiki/Duality_(mathematics)" title="Duality (mathematics)">duality</a>.  This is similar to the use of <a href="/wiki/Bra%E2%80%93ket_notation" title="Bra–ket notation">bra–ket notation</a> in quantum mechanics.  In <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_logic" title="Mathematical logic">logic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_computation" title="Theory of computation">theory of computation</a>, the function notation of <a href="/wiki/Lambda_calculus" title="Lambda calculus">lambda calculus</a> is used to explicitly express the basic notions of function <a href="/wiki/Abstraction_(computer_science)" title="Abstraction (computer science)">abstraction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Function_application" title="Function application">application</a>.  In <a href="/wiki/Category_theory" title="Category theory">category theory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Homological_algebra" title="Homological algebra">homological algebra</a>, networks of functions are described in terms of how they and their compositions <a href="/wiki/Commutative_property" title="Commutative property">commute</a> with each other using <a href="/wiki/Commutative_diagram" title="Commutative diagram">commutative diagrams</a> that extend and generalize the arrow notation for functions described above.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_terms">Other terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other terms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For broader coverage of this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Map_(mathematics)" title="Map (mathematics)">Map (mathematics)</a>.</div>
<table class="wikitable floatright" style="width: 50%">
<tbody><tr>
<th>Term
</th>
<th>Distinction from "function"
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3"><a href="/wiki/Map_(mathematics)" title="Map (mathematics)">Map/Mapping</a>
</td>
<td>None; the terms are synonymous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>A map can have <i>any set</i> as its codomain, while, in some contexts, typically in older books, the codomain of a function is specifically the set of <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real</a> or <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex</a> numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Alternatively, a map is associated with a <i>special structure</i> (e.g. by explicitly specifying a structured codomain in its definition). For example, a <a href="/wiki/Linear_map" title="Linear map">linear map</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Homomorphism" title="Homomorphism">Homomorphism</a>
</td>
<td>A function between two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Structure_(mathematics)" title="Structure (mathematics)">structures</a> of the same type that preserves the operations of the structure (e.g. a <a href="/wiki/Group_homomorphism" title="Group homomorphism">group homomorphism</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Morphism" title="Morphism">Morphism</a>
</td>
<td>A generalisation of homomorphisms to any <a href="/wiki/Category_(mathematics)" title="Category (mathematics)">category</a>, even when the objects of the category are not sets (for example, a <a href="/wiki/Group_(mathematics)" title="Group (mathematics)">group</a> defines a category with only one object, which has the elements of the group as morphisms; see <a href="/wiki/Category_(mathematics)#Examples" title="Category (mathematics)">Category (mathematics) § Examples</a> for this example and other similar ones).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A function is often also called a <b>map</b> or a <b>mapping</b>, but some authors make a distinction between the term "map" and "function". For example, the term "map" is often reserved for a "function" with some sort of special structure (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Maps_of_manifolds" title="Maps of manifolds">maps of manifolds</a>). In particular <i>map</i> is often used in place of <i>homomorphism</i> for the sake of succinctness (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Linear_map" title="Linear map">linear map</a> or <i>map from <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">G</span> to <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">H</span></i> instead of <i><a href="/wiki/Group_homomorphism" title="Group homomorphism">group homomorphism</a> from <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">G</span> to <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">H</span></i>). Some authors<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> reserve the word <i>mapping</i> for the case where the structure of the codomain belongs explicitly to the definition of the function.
</p><p>Some authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Serge_Lang" title="Serge Lang">Serge Lang</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> use "function" only to refer to maps for which the <a href="/wiki/Codomain" title="Codomain">codomain</a> is a subset of the <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real</a> or <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex</a> numbers, and use the term <i>mapping</i> for more general functions.
</p><p>In the theory of <a href="/wiki/Dynamical_system" title="Dynamical system">dynamical systems</a>, a map denotes an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discrete-time_dynamical_system" title="Discrete-time dynamical system">evolution function</a> used to create <a href="/wiki/Dynamical_system#Maps" title="Dynamical system">discrete dynamical systems</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Poincar%C3%A9_map" title="Poincaré map">Poincaré map</a>.
</p><p>Whichever definition of <i>map</i> is used, related terms like <i><a href="/wiki/Domain_of_a_function" title="Domain of a function">domain</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Codomain" title="Codomain">codomain</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Injective_function" title="Injective function">injective</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Continuous_function" title="Continuous function">continuous</a></i> have the same meaning as for a function.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifying_a_function">Specifying a function</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Specifying a function">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Given a function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, by definition, to each element <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> of the domain of the function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>

</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, there is a unique element associated to it, the value <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f(x)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/202945cce41ecebb6f643f31d119c514bec7a074" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.418ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> at <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>. There are several ways to specify or describe how <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is related to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f(x)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/202945cce41ecebb6f643f31d119c514bec7a074" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.418ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, both explicitly and implicitly. Sometimes, a theorem or an <a href="/wiki/Axiom" title="Axiom">axiom</a> asserts the existence of a function having some properties, without describing it more precisely. Often, the specification or description is referred to as the definition of the function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_listing_function_values">By listing function values</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: By listing function values">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On a finite set, a function may be defined by listing the elements of the codomain that are associated to the elements of the domain. For example, if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle A=\{1,2,3\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo>,</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>3</mn>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>

</semantics>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_a_formula">By a formula</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Function_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: By a formula">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Functions are often defined by a <a href="/wiki/Closed-form_expression" title="Closed-form expression">formula</a> that describes a combination of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arithmetic_operations" title="Arithmetic operations">arithmetic operations</a> and previously defined functions; such a formula allows computing the value of the function from the value of any element of the domain.
For example, in the above example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> can be defined by the formula <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(n)=n+1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

<mn>1</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>3</mn>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n\in \{1,2,3\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle n\in \{1,2,3\}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a7fd153aab97fa5d1cd50604f5b61c15bda65a87" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.116ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>When a function is defined this way, the determination of its domain is sometimes difficult. If the formula that defines the function contains divisions, the values of the variable for which a denominator is zero must be excluded from the domain; thus, for a complicated function, the determination of the domain passes through the computation of the <a href="/wiki/Zero_of_a_function" title="Zero of a function">zeros</a> of auxiliary functions. Similarly, if <a href="/wiki/Square_root" title="Square root">square roots</a> occur in the definition of a function from <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} ,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} ,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0522388d36b55de7babe4bbfc49475eaf590c2bd" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> the domain is included in the set of the values of the variable for which the arguments of the square roots are nonnegative.
</p><p>For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)={\sqrt {1+x^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

(In old texts, such a domain was called the <i>domain of definition</i> of the function.)
</p><p>Functions are often classified by the nature of formulas that define them:
</p>
<ul><li>A <a href="/wiki/Quadratic_function" title="Quadratic function">quadratic function</a> is a function that may be written <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)=ax^{2}+bx+c,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)=ax^{2}+bx+c,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)=ax^{2}+bx+c,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3ba19534f962564659c4c764c520a9b1c2583290" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:20.791ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> where <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i>, <i>b</i>, <i>c</i></span> are <a href="/wiki/Constant_(mathematics)" title="Constant (mathematics)">constants</a>.</li>
<li>More generally, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polynomial_function" title="Polynomial function">polynomial function</a> is a function that can be defined by a formula involving only additions, subtractions, multiplications, and <a href="/wiki/Exponentiation" title="Exponentiation">exponentiation</a> to nonnegative integers. For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)=x^{3}-3x-1,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {x-1}{x+1}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {x-1}{x+1}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1175bc3324fa6a9f39bdc801c5cfa9e59e0eace" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:14.332ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {1}{x+1}}+{\frac {3}{x}}-{\frac {2}{x-1}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
